Dialectic -- Jadal

Handling Conflicting Quranic Verses in Jadal: Naskh and Tarjih
Author describes methods of handling conflicts between two Quranic verses in jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the methods of naskh and tarjih to resolve apparent contradictions between Quranic verses in a jadal debate, and identify when a verse is general from one aspect and specific from another.

Core Idea
When Quranic verses conflict in jadal, use naskh if chronology is known, otherwise tarjih.

In jadal (dialectical debate), opponents often cite different Quranic verses to support their positions. How does a claimant respond when the objector's verse seems to contradict his own? This passage from al-Baji's work on jadal outlines the key methods: abrogation (naskh) if chronology is known, or preponderance (tarjih) if not. It also addresses a nuanced case where each verse is general in one respect and specific in another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting verses
What are the two verses in the dispute? List the claimant's verse and the objector's verse. Note their apparent conflict.
In the Maliki example, the claimant's verse prohibits combining two sisters; the objector's verse permits what right hands possess.
2
Check for abrogation (naskh)
Determine if one verse is known to be later in revelation. If so, the later abrogates the earlier, resolving the conflict.
The author says: 'Īn لم يعرف التاريخ رجح الحكم بأحدهما' — if chronology is unknown, proceed to tarjih.
3
If chronology unknown, seek preponderance (tarjih)
Look for criteria to give one verse weight over the other, such as directness to the ruling, specificity, or intent of the verse.
Tarjih can be based on which verse is more specific to the disputed matter.
4
Analyse the 'amm min wajh, khass min wajh' case
When each verse is general in one way and specific in another, identify which verse is more specific to the disputed ruling. The verse that directly addresses the disputed point is given preponderance.
The Maliki's verse is specific to sisters, the opponent's is general to all right hand possessions; the claimant's verse wins because it directly addresses the ruling in dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني : أن يقول بنسخ الآية الأولى بالثانية بأن يقول : آيتنا متأخرة وآيتكم متقدمة، وذلك أن آيتكم نزلت في بدر وآيتنا نزلت بعدها .
والثالث : أن يرجح استعمال آيته على آيتهم ببعض أنواع الترجيح، إن وجد إلى ذلك سيلا

فإن كانا خاصين لا يمكن استعمالهما معا، ورغم أن هذا النوع نادر جدا، إلا أن الطريق في الجواب عليه إن وجد أن ينسخ الدليل الأول بالآخر منهما، وإن لم يعرف التاريخ رجح الحكم بأحدهما على الحكم بالآخر بوجه من وجوه الترجيح .

ج - 3 – وإن كان كل واحد منهما عامًا من وجه خاصا من وجه وذلك مثل أن يستدل المالكي على أنه لا يجمع بين الأختين بملك اليمين بقوله تعالى: ... وَأَن تَجْمَعُوا بَيْنَ الأُختين . . . ) ، ولم يفرق بين النكاح وبين اليمين . وهنا يعارضه المخالف بقوله تعالى : .. وما مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَنُكُمْ ... (2) ولم يفرق بين الأختين وغيرهما، فليس للمستدل أن يحمل آية المعترض على غير الأختين بأن آيته خاصة في الأختين، إلا وللمعترض أن يحمل آية المستدل على غير ملك اليمين بأن آيته خاصة في ملك اليمين والطريق في الجواب عن مثل هذا الاعتراض، إن وقع أن يرجح المستدل استعمال آيته على آية المعترض، وذلك بأن يقول : في هذا الموضع استعمال آيتنا أولى لأنه قصد بها بيان ما أبيح جمعه في النكاح وما منع منه ، وآيتكم إنما قصد بها بيان الحالة التي أجيز فيها نكاح الإماء، والآية التي قصد بها بيان الحكم المختلف فيه أولى من الآية التي لم يقصد بها ذلك
The second: That he says by abrogating the first verse with the second, saying: Our verse is later and your verse is earlier, and that is because your verse was revealed at Badr and our verse was revealed after it. The third: That he gives preponderance to the use of his verse over their verse by some type of preponderance, if a way to that is found. If they are both specific such that they cannot both be applied, and although this type is very rare, the way to answer it, if found, is to abrogate the first proof with the latter of the two, and if the chronology is not known, the ruling of one is given preponderance over the ruling of the other by some aspect of preponderance. C - 3 - And if each one is general in one aspect and specific in another, such as when the Maliki argues that one cannot combine two sisters by right hand possession by His saying: '...and that you combine between the two sisters...' and he did not differentiate between marriage and possession. Here the opponent opposes him by His saying: '...and what your right hands possess...' and he did not differentiate between sisters and others. So the claimant cannot interpret the opponent's verse as other than sisters, saying his verse is specific to sisters, without the opponent being able to interpret the claimant's verse as other than right hand possession, saying his verse is specific to right hand possession. The way to answer such an objection, if it occurs, is that the claimant gives preponderance to the use of his verse over the opponent's verse, by saying: In this situation, the use of our verse is more appropriate because it intended to clarify what is permitted to combine in marriage and what is prohibited, while your verse only intended to clarify the situation in which marriage to slave women is permitted, and the verse intended to clarify the ruling in dispute is more appropriate than the verse not intended for that.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a classification of methods for handling objections (naqd) in jadal when both sides rely on Quranic verses. The author, presumably al-Baji from the referenced work, presents three scenarios. The second method is abrogation (naskh): the later verse abrogates the earlier one, so the claimant claims his verse is later. The third method is preponderance (tarjih): without known chronology, one gives weight to one verse over another by some criteria. Then the author discusses a special case: both verses are specific in one aspect and general in another. He gives an example: the Maliki cites the prohibition of combining two sisters (general? implying marriage and possession) and the opponent cites permission of what right hands possess (not distinguishing sisters). The solution is preponderance based on which verse more directly addresses the disputed ruling. The passage teaches that in jadal, when verses conflict, one must use abrogation (if chronology known) or preponderance (otherwise), and when each verse has a specific application, the claimant's verse that specifically addresses the disputed point is preferred.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of an earlier verse by a later one, used to resolve contradiction by establishing chronological priority.
ترجيح (tarjih): Giving preponderance to one proof over another based on some criteria (e.g., more specific, clearer purpose).
عام ('amm): General term that includes multiple individuals; here applied to a verse that does not differentiate between categories.
خاص (khass): Specific term that refers to a particular subset; here a verse limited to a specific ruling or situation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proper response when two specific verses cannot both be applied and the chronology is unknown?
A) Abrogate both verses
B) Give preponderance to one ruling over the other by some aspect of tarjih
C) Reject both verses as contradictory
D) Accept the first verses mentioned

Key Takeaway
When Quranic verses conflict in jadal, use naskh if chronology is known, otherwise tarjih; when verses are each general and specific, the verse that more directly addresses the disputed ruling is given preponderance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a jadal exchange: Claimant argues that riba includes credit sales using hadith 'every loan that brings benefit is riba'; Objector counters that general permission for trade (Quran 2:275) allows it. Use either naskh or tarjih to resolve, and explain your reasoning.
?
In a debate about the permissibility of tawarruq, one side cites a hadith prohibiting bay' al-gharar, the other cites a general permission for trade. Identify whether the case falls under the 'amm min wajh, khass min wajh' scenario and decide which verse should be given preponderance.

Nass and Qiyas: The Absolute Barrier
Author explains the case of nass in jadal opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a nass cannot be opposed by qiyas in a jadal exchange.

Core Idea
A nass is the final word – qiyas cannot overturn it.

In jadal, when a claimant cites a Quranic verse that is unequivocal (nass), any objection based on analogy is automatically invalid. This lesson explains why and gives the standard response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nass
Locate the verse in the argument that is presented as a nass. In the example, the Maliki cites Quran 5:5 regarding marriage to free Kitabiyya women. A nass is a text that cannot be interpreted differently.
2
Recognize the opponent's qiyas
The opponent uses an analogy to challenge the nass. Here, the opponent argues that a free Kitabiyya woman is like a slave Kitabiyya in that she is a disbeliever, so marriage is not permissible. This is an attempt to oppose the nass with qiyas.
3
Remember the consensus rule
The author states there is no disagreement among scholars that a nass from the Book cannot be opposed by qiyas or any other evidence. This is a settled principle.
4
Apply the response
The claimant's response is to reject the qiyas outright, stating that opposing the Book with qiyas is not permissible. This ends the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني : المعارضة بعلة قياس
بمعنى أن يستدل المدعي لرأيه بآية من القرآن فيعارضه السائل بقياس، وفي هذه الحالة لا يخلو أن تكون الآية المستدل بها : نصا لا يحتمل التأويل، أو ظاهرًا يحتمل التأويل، أو عموما يحتمل التخصيص.
أ - أن تكون نصا لا يحتمل التأويل
وذلك مثل أن يستدل المالكي على جواز نكاح حرائر أهل الكتاب بقوله تعالى : (وَالْمُحْصَنَتُ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ إِذَا اتَيْتُمُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ...) (1) . فيعارضه من يذهب إلى أن هذه كافرة فلا يجوز نكاحها إذا كانت أمة ، فيقول المالكي مجيبا : هذه معارضة الكتاب بالقياس، وذلك غير جائز، ولا خلاف بين أهل العلم في أنه لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة.
ب - أن تكون ظاهرا يحتمل التأويل :
مثل أن يستدل المالكي على وجوب السكنى للمطلقة المبتوتة بقوله عز وجل : أَنكِنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَتُم مِّن وُجْدِكُمْ ...) (2) . فيعارضه الحنبلي بأن يقول : أحمله على الندب، بدليل أن من لا تجب لها النفقة لا يجب لها السكنى كالأجنبية.
والطريق في الجواب أن يقول المالكي: إن النفقة في مقابلة التمكين من الاستمتاع والمبتوتة غير ممكنة، فلذلك لم تجب لها النفقة، وليس كذلك هذا فإنه لحرز النسب وحفظه، فكأنه أشبه العدة .
ج - أن تكون عاما يحتمل التخصيص :
مثل استدلال المالكي على أن الحر إذا عدم الطول أو خاف العنت، جاز له أربع إماء، لقوله تعالى : فانكحوا ما طاب لكم مِّنَ النِّسَاء مَثْنَى وَثُلث وَرُبَعَ) (3) . فيعترض الشافعي قائلا : هذا مخصوص بالقياس، وهو أن هذا حر
The second section: Opposing with analogical reasoning.
Meaning that the claimant argues for his opinion with a verse from the Quran, and the questioner opposes him with an analogy. In this case, the verse cited is either: a text (nass) that does not admit interpretation (ta'wil), or an apparent (zahir) that admits interpretation, or a general ('amm) that admits specification (takhsis).
A - That it is a nass that does not admit interpretation:
Such as when the Maliki argues for the permissibility of marrying free women of the People of the Book by His saying: 'And the chaste ones from those who were given the Scripture before you, when you give them their rewards...' (5:5). The opponent who holds that she is a disbeliever and so marriage is not permissible if she is a slave woman opposes him. The Maliki responds: This is opposing the Book with analogy, and that is not permissible, and there is no disagreement among the people of knowledge that it is not permissible to oppose a nass from the Book with analogy or other evidences.
B - That it is a zahir that admits interpretation:
Such as when the Maliki argues for the obligation of housing for the irrevocably divorced woman by His saying: 'House them from where you dwell...' (65:6). The Hanbali opposes him by saying: I interpret it as recommendation, by the evidence that whoever is not entitled to maintenance is not entitled to housing, like a foreign woman. The way to answer is that the Maliki says: Maintenance is in exchange for enabling enjoyment, and the irrevocably divorced woman is not capable of that, so maintenance is not obligatory for her, but this is not the case, for it is for the protection of lineage and preservation, so it resembles the waiting period ('iddah).
C - That it is a general that admits specification:
Such as the Maliki's argument that a free man, if he lacks wealth or fears hardship, may marry four slave women, by His saying: 'Marry what seems good to you of women, two, three, or four' (4:3). The Shafi'i objects saying: This is specified by analogy, namely that this free man...
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage introduces a new type of objection in jadal: when the claimant cites a Quranic verse and the opponent counters with a qiyas (analogy). The author classifies the verse into three categories: nass (unequivocal text), zahir (apparent but open to interpretation), and 'amm (general). For the nass, the claimant's response is to reject the analogy outright, as nass cannot be opposed by qiyas—this is a settled principle among scholars. For the zahir, the opponent may interpret it differently (e.g., as recommendation), and the claimant must respond by distinguishing the situation: in the example of housing for the irrevocably divorced woman, the Maliki argues that housing is not for enjoyment but for preserving lineage, so it is analogous to 'iddah, not to a foreign woman who lacks maintenance. For the general, the opponent may argue that qiyas specifies it, as in the marriage to slave women: the Shafi'i says the general command is specified by an analogy that a free man is limited to four free women or can marry slave women only under conditions. The passage thus teaches how to handle each type when argued.

Key Terms
نص
قياس
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how should a claimant respond when his cited verse is a nass (unequivocal) and the opponent uses qiyas?
A) Reject the qiyas by showing it contradicts a stronger qiyas
B) Accept the qiyas if it is logically sound
C) Reject the qiyas outright because nass cannot be opposed by qiyas or any other evidence
D) Interpret the nass to accommodate the qiyas

Key Takeaway
A nass (unequivocal text) cannot be opposed by qiyas; any such objection is automatically invalid per scholarly consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Write a short response (1-2 sentences) a Maliki jurist could give when someone tries to use qiyas to argue against the permissibility of marrying free Kitabiyya women, based on the nass rule.
?
Identify another nass from the Quran (e.g., a clear inheritance share) and explain why an opponent cannot use qiyas to challenge it.

Zahir Verses: Defending Against Qiyas via Distinction
Author explains the case of zahir in jadal opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a response when an opponent uses qiyas to reinterpret a zahir verse.

Core Idea
A zahir can be interpreted, but the claimant can defend it by distinguishing the effective cause.

When a verse is zahir (apparent but open to interpretation), an opponent may use qiyas to argue for a different meaning. The claimant must then show that the analogy is flawed by pointing out a difference in the underlying cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse as zahir
In the example, the Maliki cites Quran 65:6 about housing for divorced women. The verse's apparent meaning is obligatory, but it admits interpretation, so it is zahir.
2
Recognize the opponent's reinterpretation via qiyas
The Hanbali opponent argues that the verse should be interpreted as recommendation (not obligation) based on qiyas with a foreign woman (ajnabiyya): since a foreign woman is not entitled to maintenance or housing, the divorced woman is similar, so housing is not obligatory.
3
Distinguish the effective cause ('illah)
The claimant must show that the 'illah in the original case (housing for the divorced woman) is different from the 'illah in the analogized case. The Maliki says: maintenance is in exchange for sexual availability, which the divorced woman lacks, so she gets no maintenance. But housing is for the protection of lineage and preservation of the child, so it is like the 'iddah period, which is obligatory.
4
Formulate the response
The claimant's answer should make this distinction clear and argue that the qiyas fails because the 'illah are different.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) . فيعارضه من يذهب إلى أن هذه كافرة فلا يجوز نكاحها إذا كانت أمة ، فيقول المالكي مجيبا : هذه معارضة الكتاب بالقياس، وذلك غير جائز، ولا خلاف بين أهل العلم في أنه لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة.

What is the key difference the Maliki uses to defend housing for the divorced woman against the Hanbali's qiyas?

General Verses and Specification by Qiyas
Author explains the case of 'amm in jadal opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a general verse is specified by qiyas and how a claimant may respond.

Core Idea
A general ('amm) can be specified by qiyas, but the claimant can argue the specification is invalid.

A general term in a verse can be restricted in scope by a qiyas. The claimant must then argue either that the qiyas is weak or that the general rule remains applicable despite the analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse as 'amm
In the example, the Maliki uses Quran 4:3 which permits marrying 'what seems good' of women, up to four. The phrase 'women' is general and includes free and slave women.
2
Recognize the opponent's use of qiyas to specify
The Shafi'i opponent argues that the general verse is specified by qiyas: a free man is limited by the general rules of marriage, so he can only marry free women or slave women under certain conditions. The qiyas narrows the general rule.
3
Formulate a response
The claimant can argue that the qiyas is not strong enough to specify the general, or that the general rule is clear and the qiyas contradicts a stronger principle. The passage does not give the full response, but the claimant might say the qiyas is invalid because the 'illah is not applicable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني : المعارضة بعلة قياس
بمعنى أن يستدل المدعي لرأيه بآية من القرآن فيعارضه السائل بقياس، وفي هذه الحالة لا يخلو أن تكون الآية المستدل بها : نصا لا يحتمل التأويل، أو ظاهرًا يحتمل التأويل، أو عموما يحتمل التخصيص.
أ - أن تكون نصا لا يحتمل التأويل
وذلك مثل أن يستدل المالكي على جواز نكاح حرائر أهل الكتاب بقوله تعالى : (وَالْمُحْصَنَتُ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ إِذَا اتَيْتُمُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ...) (1) . فيعارضه من يذهب إلى أن هذه كافرة فلا يجوز نكاحها إذا كانت أمة ، فيقول المالكي مجيبا : هذه معارضة الكتاب بالقياس، وذلك غير جائز، ولا خلاف بين أهل العلم في أنه لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة.
ب - أن تكون ظاهرا يحتمل التأويل :
مثل أن يستدل المالكي على وجوب السكنى للمطلقة المبتوتة بقوله عز وجل : أَنكِنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَتُم مِّن وُجْدِكُمْ ...) (2) . فيعارضه الحنبلي بأن يقول : أحمله على الندب، بدليل أن من لا تجب لها النفقة لا يجب لها السكنى كالأجنبية.
والطريق في الجواب أن يقول المالكي: إن النفقة في مقابلة التمكين من الاستمتاع والمبتوتة غير ممكنة، فلذلك لم تجب لها النفقة، وليس كذلك هذا فإنه لحرز النسب وحفظه، فكأنه أشبه العدة .
ج - أن تكون عاما يحتمل التخصيص :
مثل استدلال المالكي على أن الحر إذا عدم الطول أو خاف العنت، جاز له أربع إماء، لقوله تعالى : فانكحوا ما طاب لكم مِّنَ النِّسَاء مَثْنَى وَثُلث وَرُبَعَ) (3) . فيعترض الشافعي قائلا : هذا مخصوص بالقياس، وهو أن هذا حر
The second section: Opposing with analogical reasoning.
Meaning that the claimant argues for his opinion with a verse from the Quran, and the questioner opposes him with an analogy. In this case, the verse cited is either: a text (nass) that does not admit interpretation (ta'wil), or an apparent (zahir) that admits interpretation, or a general ('amm) that admits specification (takhsis).
A - That it is a nass that does not admit interpretation:
Such as when the Maliki argues for the permissibility of marrying free women of the People of the Book by His saying: 'And the chaste ones from those who were given the Scripture before you, when you give them their rewards...' (5:5). The opponent who holds that she is a disbeliever and so marriage is not permissible if she is a slave woman opposes him. The Maliki responds: This is opposing the Book with analogy, and that is not permissible, and there is no disagreement among the people of knowledge that it is not permissible to oppose a nass from the Book with analogy or other evidences.
B - That it is a zahir that admits interpretation:
Such as when the Maliki argues for the obligation of housing for the irrevocably divorced woman by His saying: 'House them from where you dwell...' (65:6). The Hanbali opposes him by saying: I interpret it as recommendation, by the evidence that whoever is not entitled to maintenance is not entitled to housing, like a foreign woman. The way to answer is that the Maliki says: Maintenance is in exchange for enabling enjoyment, and the irrevocably divorced woman is not capable of that, so maintenance is not obligatory for her, but this is not the case, for it is for the protection of lineage and preservation, so it resembles the waiting period ('iddah).
C - That it is a general that admits specification:
Such as the Maliki's argument that a free man, if he lacks wealth or fears hardship, may marry four slave women, by His saying: 'Marry what seems good to you of women, two, three, or four' (4:3). The Shafi'i objects saying: This is specified by analogy, namely that this free man...
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage introduces a new type of objection in jadal: when the claimant cites a Quranic verse and the opponent counters with a qiyas (analogy). The author classifies the verse into three categories: nass (unequivocal text), zahir (apparent but open to interpretation), and 'amm (general). For the nass, the claimant's response is to reject the analogy outright, as nass cannot be opposed by qiyas—this is a settled principle among scholars. For the zahir, the opponent may interpret it differently (e.g., as recommendation), and the claimant must respond by distinguishing the situation: in the example of housing for the irrevocably divorced woman, the Maliki argues that housing is not for enjoyment but for preserving lineage, so it is analogous to 'iddah, not to a foreign woman who lacks maintenance. For the general, the opponent may argue that qiyas specifies it, as in the marriage to slave women: the Shafi'i says the general command is specified by an analogy that a free man is limited to four free women or can marry slave women only under conditions. The passage thus teaches how to handle each type when argued.

Key Terms
عام
تخصيص
قياس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what type of verse can be specified by qiyas?
A) Nass (unequivocal)
B) Zahir (apparent)
C) 'Amm (general)
D) Both nass and zahir

Key Takeaway
A general verse can be specified by qiyas, but the claimant can challenge the specification by questioning the strength of the analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
State in one sentence the Shafi'i objection to the Maliki's claim, based on the passage.
?
Propose a possible Maliki response defending the generality of the verse, using the concept that qiyas cannot override a clear general unless it is very strong.

Dialectic -- Jadal
beginner

The Three Types of Quranic Evidence in Jadal
Author introduces three types and the rule for nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Quranic evidence into nass, zahir, and 'amm, and explain the rule that nass cannot be countered by qiyas.

Core Idea
Clear text (nass) is immune to qiyas; only probable and general texts can be contested.

In dialectical encounters (jadal), a claimant may adduce a Quranic verse to support his position. The opponent may counter with analogical reasoning (qiyas). This lesson introduces the three categories of Quranic evidence that determine whether such a counter is permissible. Understanding this classification is essential for evaluating the strength of arguments in Islamic legal debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of evidence
Look at the passage: the author lists nass (clear text), zahir (probable text), and 'amm (general text). Each has different susceptibility to counter-arguments.
2
Understand the immunity of nass
The passage states that nass is 'not susceptible to interpretation'. Any counter with qiyas is unanimously invalid. Note the Maliki example with Qur'an 5:5.
3
Recognize that qiyas is invalid against nass
The author says: 'لا خلاف بين أهل العلم في أنه لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة' – there is no disagreement that it is impermissible to counter the clear text with qiyas or any other evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني : المعارضة بعلة قياس
بمعنى أن يستدل المدعي لرأيه بآية من القرآن فيعارضه السائل بقياس، وفي هذه الحالة لا يخلو أن تكون الآية المستدل بها : نصا لا يحتمل التأويل، أو ظاهرًا يحتمل التأويل، أو عموما يحتمل التخصيص.
أ - أن تكون نصا لا يحتمل التأويل
وذلك مثل أن يستدل المالكي على جواز نكاح حرائر أهل الكتاب بقوله تعالى : (وَالْمُحْصَنَتُ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ إِذَا اتَيْتُمُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ...) . فيعارضه من يذهب إلى أن هذه كافرة فلا يجوز نكاحها إذا كانت أمة ، فيقول المالكي مجيبا : هذه معارضة الكتاب بالقياس، وذلك غير جائز، ولا خلاف بين أهل العلم في أنه لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة. ب - أن تكون ظاهرا يحتمل التأويل :
مثل أن يستدل المالكي على وجوب السكنى للمطلقة المبتوتة بقوله عز وجل : أَنكِنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَتُم مِّن وُجْدِكُمْ ...) . فيعارضه الحنبلي بأن يقول : أحمله على الندب، بدليل أن من لا تجب لها النفقة لا يجب لها السكنى كالأجنبية.
والطريق في الجواب أن يقول المالكي: إن النفقة في مقابلة التمكين من الاستمتاع والمبتوتة غير ممكنة، فلذلك لم تجب لها النفقة، وليس كذلك هذا فإنه لحرز النسب وحفظه، فكأنه أشبه العدة .
ج - أن تكون عاما يحتمل التخصيص : مثل استدلال المالكي على أن الحر إذا عدم الطول أو خاف العنت، جاز له أربع إماء، لقوله تعالى : فانكحوا ما طاب لكم مِّنَ النِّسَاء مَثْنَى وَثُلث وَرُبَعَ) فيعترض الشافعي قائلا : هذا مخصوص بالقياس، وهو أن هذا حر متمسك بنكاح ، فلم يجز نكاح أمة كما لو كانت تحته حرة.
والطريق في الجواب عن ذلك أن يتكلم المالكي على القياس، بأن يقول مثلا بعدم جواز ابتداء تأويل الظاهر ولا تخصيص العموم بالقياس، لكن الباجي يرى أن هذا النوع من الجواب ليس بصحيح
The Second Section: The Counter-argument with the Cause of Qiyas. Meaning that the claimant adduces for his opinion a verse from the Quran, then the questioner counters it with a qiyas (analogical reasoning). In this case, the verse adduced is either: a clear text (nass) not susceptible to interpretation, or a probable text (zahir) susceptible to interpretation, or a general text ('amm) susceptible to specification.
A - That it be a clear text not susceptible to interpretation. An example is that a Maliki adduces the permissibility of marrying free women of the People of the Book by His statement the Exalted: "And [lawful to you are] the chaste from among those who were given the Scripture before you, when you have given them their due compensation..." So the one who holds that she is a disbeliever and thus it is not permissible to marry her if she is a slave counters him. So the Maliki responds: This is a counter-argument against the Book by qiyas, and that is not permissible. There is no disagreement among the people of knowledge that it is not permissible to counter the clear text of the Book by qiyas or by any other evidence.
B - That it be a probable text susceptible to interpretation: An example is that a Maliki adduces the obligation of dwelling for the irrevocably divorced woman by His statement the Exalted: "Lodge them [in a part] of where you dwell out of your means..." So a Hanbali counters him by saying: I carry it upon recommendation, by evidence that one who does not have obligatory maintenance does not have obligatory dwelling, like a foreign woman. The method in the answer is that the Maliki says: Indeed, maintenance is in exchange for enabling enjoyment, and the irrevocably divorced woman is not enabled, therefore maintenance is not obligatory for her. But this is not the case; because it is for the preservation of lineage and its protection, so it is as if it resembles the waiting period ('idda).
C - That it be a general text susceptible to specification: An example is the Maliki's argument that a free man, if he lacks the means or fears hardship, may marry four slave women, by His statement: "Then marry what is good to you of women: two, three, or four." So the Shafi'i objects saying: This is specified by qiyas, which is that this is a free man holding to marriage, so it is not permissible to marry a slave woman just as if he had a free wife under him. The method in answering that is that the Maliki discusses the qiyas, for example by saying that it is not permissible to initiate interpretation of the probable text nor specification of the general text by qiyas. However, al-Baji holds that this type of answer is not correct.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from 'Jadal Usuliyyin' explains a key dialectical technique: how to respond when an opponent counters a Quranic proof with an analogical argument (qiyas). The author classifies the Quranic evidence into three types: clear text (nass), probable text (zahir), and general text ('amm). For each, the author provides a concrete example from madhhab disputes and the proper dialectical response.

First, if the verse is a clear text (nass) that admits no interpretation, any counter with qiyas is invalid. The example: a Maliki cites Qur'an 5:5 to permit marrying free women of the People of the Book. The opponent counters that a believing free woman is better, but the Maliki responds that countering the clear text of the Book with qiyas is unanimously impermissible.

Second, if the verse is a probable text (zahir) open to interpretation, the opponent may offer an alternative interpretation. The example: a Maliki uses Qur'an 65:6 to argue that an irrevocably divorced woman deserves dwelling. The Hanbali counters that it is only recommended, using qiyas: a woman without maintenance does not get dwelling, like a stranger. The proper response is to distinguish the 'illa (cause): dwelling is for lineage preservation, not in exchange for enjoyment like maintenance, so it resembles the 'idda.

Third, if the verse is general ('amm) open to specification, the opponent may use qiyas to specify it. The example: a Maliki uses Qur'an 4:3 to allow a free man to marry slave women. The Shafi'i specifies it by qiyas: a free man married to a free woman cannot marry a slave woman. The proper response is to discuss the qiyas itself, arguing that one cannot initiate specification of a general text with qiyas. However, the author notes that al-Baji considers this last response unsound.

Throughout, the passage illustrates the nuanced rules of jadal where the authority of textual evidence constrains the use of analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
المعارضة
القياس
النص
الظاهر
العام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of Quranic verse cannot be countered by qiyas at all?
A) The clear text (nass) that does not admit interpretation
B) The probable text (zahir) that admits interpretation
C) The general text ('amm) that admits specification
D) All of the above can be countered

Key Takeaway
Quranic nass overrides any analogical reasoning; it is invulnerable to qiyas.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given a Quranic verse, classify it as nass, zahir, or 'amm, and decide whether a qiyas argument can be used against it. For example, consider Qur'an 24:2 (the verse on flogging for adultery): is it nass or zahir? Justify your answer.
?
In a debate simulation, take the position of a Maliki and respond to an opponent who uses qiyas to challenge a nass verse you adduced.

Dialectic -- Jadal
intermediate

Responding to Qiyas Against a Zahir Verse
Author gives example of Maliki vs Hanbali on dwelling for irrevocably divorced woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a dialectical response when a probable verse (zahir) is countered by qiyas, by distinguishing the 'illa (effective cause).

Core Idea
A probable text can be defended by showing that the qiyas's 'illa does not apply.

When the adduced verse is probable (zahir), the opponent may offer an alternative interpretation supported by qiyas. The defender must respond by demonstrating that the analogy's underlying cause ( 'illa) is not present in the verse's context. This lesson walks through a concrete example from the Maliki-Hanbali dispute on dwelling for the irrevocably divorced woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse as zahir
The passage says that the verse on lodging (Qur'an 65:6) is zahir because it can be interpreted as obligatory or recommended. Recognize that it is not definitive.
2
Identify the opponent's qiyas and its 'illa
The Hanbali uses qiyas: a woman without maintenance (like a foreign woman) does not have obligatory dwelling. The 'illa is that dwelling is tied to maintenance.
3
Formulate a response by distinguishing the 'illa
The Maliki argues that maintenance is in exchange for enjoyment, but dwelling for the divorced woman is for preservation of lineage, similar to 'idda. Thus the 'illa of the qiyas does not apply.
This is a classic move in jadal: rebutting an analogy by showing a difference in the 'illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Second Section: The Counter-argument with the Cause of Qiyas. Meaning that the claimant adduces for his opinion a verse from the Quran, then the questioner counters it with a qiyas (analogical reasoning). In this case, the verse adduced is either: a clear text (nass) not susceptible to interpretation, or a probable text (zahir) susceptible to interpretation, or a general text ('amm) susceptible to specification.

Commentary
This passage from 'Jadal Usuliyyin' explains a key dialectical technique: how to respond when an opponent counters a Quranic proof with an analogical argument (qiyas). The author classifies the Quranic evidence into three types: clear text (nass), probable text (zahir), and general text ('amm). However, the author notes that al-Baji considers this last response unsound.

Throughout, the passage illustrates the nuanced rules of jadal where the authority of textual evidence constrains the use of analogical reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a debate, your opponent uses qiyas to argue that a probable verse (zahir) should be interpreted as recommended rather than obligatory. Construct a response by identifying a difference in the 'illa, using the example from this lesson as a model.
?
Given a hypothetical: a verse (zahir) seems to obligate Zakat on horses. An opponent argues by qiyas that horses are like donkeys (no Zakat) because both are working animals. How would you respond by distinguishing the 'illa?

Responding to Qiyas Against a 'Amm Verse
Author gives Maliki vs Shafi'i on marrying slave women, with discussion of specification by qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to argue that a general text ('amm) should not be specified by qiyas, and evaluate al-Baji's objection to that position.

Core Idea
Specifying a general text with qiyas is contested; some scholars reject it entirely.

When the adduced verse is general ('amm), the opponent may try to specify it using qiyas. The responder may argue that such specification is not permissible at all. However, as the passage notes, this response is controversial. This lesson examines the dispute and al-Baji's critique.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the verse as 'amm
The verse 'marry what is good to you of women' (Qur'an 4:3) is general, applying to free and slave women. It is open to specification.
2
Understand the opponent's qiyas for specification
The Shafi'i specifies the verse using qiyas: a free man married to a free woman cannot marry a slave woman, so the general permission is limited. This qiyas is based on the 'illa of having a free wife.
3
Learn the response that one cannot initiate takhsis with qiyas
The Maliki responds by saying that specification of a general text by qiyas is not permissible at the outset. This is a substantive position in usul al-fiqh.
4
Note al-Baji's critique
The author quotes al-Baji, who considers this type of response not correct. Reflect on why al-Baji might object – perhaps because some scholars do allow takhsis by qiyas.

المطلب الثاني : المعارضة بعلة قياس
بمعنى أن يستدل المدعي لرأيه بآية من القرآن فيعارضه السائل بقياس، وفي هذه الحالة لا يخلو أن تكون الآية المستدل بها : نصا لا يحتمل التأويل، أو ظاهرًا يحتمل التأويل، أو عموما يحتمل التخصيص.
أ - أن تكون نصا لا يحتمل التأويل
وذلك مثل أن يستدل المالكي على جواز نكاح حرائر أهل الكتاب بقوله تعالى : (وَالْمُحْصَنَتُ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ إِذَا اتَيْتُمُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ...) . فيعارضه من يذهب إلى أن هذه كافرة فلا يجوز نكاحها إذا كانت أمة ، فيقول المالكي مجيبا : هذه معارضة الكتاب بالقياس، وذلك غير جائز، ولا خلاف بين أهل العلم في أنه لا يجوز معارضة نص الكتاب بالقياس ولا بغيره من الأدلة. ب - أن تكون ظاهرا يحتمل التأويل :
مثل أن يستدل المالكي على وجوب السكنى للمطلقة المبتوتة بقوله عز وجل : أَنكِنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَتُم مِّن وُجْدِكُمْ ...) . فيعارضه الحنبلي بأن يقول : أحمله على الندب، بدليل أن من لا تجب لها النفقة لا يجب لها السكنى كالأجنبية.
والطريق في الجواب أن يقول المالكي: إن النفقة في مقابلة التمكين من الاستمتاع والمبتوتة غير ممكنة، فلذلك لم تجب لها النفقة، وليس كذلك هذا فإنه لحرز النسب وحفظه، فكأنه أشبه العدة .
ج - أن تكون عاما يحتمل التخصيص : مثل استدلال المالكي على أن الحر إذا عدم الطول أو خاف العنت، جاز له أربع إماء، لقوله تعالى : فانكحوا ما طاب لكم مِّنَ النِّسَاء مَثْنَى وَثُلث وَرُبَعَ) فيعترض الشافعي قائلا : هذا مخصوص بالقياس، وهو أن هذا حر متمسك بنكاح ، فلم يجز نكاح أمة كما لو كانت تحته حرة.
والطريق في الجواب عن ذلك أن يتكلم المالكي على القياس، بأن يقول مثلا بعدم جواز ابتداء تأويل الظاهر ولا تخصيص العموم بالقياس، لكن الباجي يرى أن هذا النوع من الجواب ليس بصحيح
The Second Section: The Counter-argument with the Cause of Qiyas. Meaning that the claimant adduces for his opinion a verse from the Quran, then the questioner counters it with a qiyas (analogical reasoning). In this case, the verse adduced is either: a clear text (nass) not susceptible to interpretation, or a probable text (zahir) susceptible to interpretation, or a general text ('amm) susceptible to specification.
A - That it be a clear text not susceptible to interpretation. An example is that a Maliki adduces the permissibility of marrying free women of the People of the Book by His statement the Exalted: "And [lawful to you are] the chaste from among those who were given the Scripture before you, when you have given them their due compensation..." So the one who holds that she is a disbeliever and thus it is not permissible to marry her if she is a slave counters him. So the Maliki responds: This is a counter-argument against the Book by qiyas, and that is not permissible. There is no disagreement among the people of knowledge that it is not permissible to counter the clear text of the Book by qiyas or by any other evidence.
B - That it be a probable text susceptible to interpretation: An example is that a Maliki adduces the obligation of dwelling for the irrevocably divorced woman by His statement the Exalted: "Lodge them [in a part] of where you dwell out of your means..." So a Hanbali counters him by saying: I carry it upon recommendation, by evidence that one who does not have obligatory maintenance does not have obligatory dwelling, like a foreign woman. The method in the answer is that the Maliki says: Indeed, maintenance is in exchange for enabling enjoyment, and the irrevocably divorced woman is not enabled, therefore maintenance is not obligatory for her. But this is not the case; because it is for the preservation of lineage and its protection, so it is as if it resembles the waiting period ('idda).
C - That it be a general text susceptible to specification: An example is the Maliki's argument that a free man, if he lacks the means or fears hardship, may marry four slave women, by His statement: "Then marry what is good to you of women: two, three, or four." So the Shafi'i objects saying: This is specified by qiyas, which is that this is a free man holding to marriage, so it is not permissible to marry a slave woman just as if he had a free wife under him. The method in answering that is that the Maliki discusses the qiyas, for example by saying that it is not permissible to initiate interpretation of the probable text nor specification of the general text by qiyas. However, al-Baji holds that this type of answer is not correct.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from 'Jadal Usuliyyin' explains a key dialectical technique: how to respond when an opponent counters a Quranic proof with an analogical argument (qiyas). The author classifies the Quranic evidence into three types: clear text (nass), probable text (zahir), and general text ('amm). For each, the author provides a concrete example from madhhab disputes and the proper dialectical response.

First, if the verse is a clear text (nass) that admits no interpretation, any counter with qiyas is invalid. The example: a Maliki cites Qur'an 5:5 to permit marrying free women of the People of the Book. The opponent counters that a believing free woman is better, but the Maliki responds that countering the clear text of the Book with qiyas is unanimously impermissible.

Second, if the verse is a probable text (zahir) open to interpretation, the opponent may offer an alternative interpretation. The example: a Maliki uses Qur'an 65:6 to argue that an irrevocably divorced woman deserves dwelling. The Hanbali counters that it is only recommended, using qiyas: a woman without maintenance does not get dwelling, like a stranger. The proper response is to distinguish the 'illa (cause): dwelling is for lineage preservation, not in exchange for enjoyment like maintenance, so it resembles the 'idda.

Third, if the verse is general ('amm) open to specification, the opponent may use qiyas to specify it. The example: a Maliki uses Qur'an 4:3 to allow a free man to marry slave women. The Shafi'i specifies it by qiyas: a free man married to a free woman cannot marry a slave woman. The proper response is to discuss the qiyas itself, arguing that one cannot initiate specification of a general text with qiyas. However, the author notes that al-Baji considers this last response unsound.

Throughout, the passage illustrates the nuanced rules of jadal where the authority of textual evidence constrains the use of analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
العام
التخصيص
القياس
ابتداء التأويل

Key Takeaway
Rejecting specification by qiyas is a valid move but not universally accepted; al-Baji considers it unsound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Analyzing a Dialectical Exchange on Qiyas
Dialectical exchange on qiyas in marriage case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a dialectical exchange in usul al-fiqh by identifying the claimant's argument, the respondent's objection, and the critic's assessment.

Core Idea
Not every response in dialectic is valid; al-Baji shows methodological rigor.

In this passage, you will witness a typical dialectical exchange from the usul tradition. A legal analogy (qiyas) regarding marriage is presented, then a Maliki scholar responds by invoking methodological rules, and finally al-Baji critiques that response. This illustrates how debates in usul al-fiqh are governed by agreed-upon procedures and how scholars evaluate each other's dialectical moves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimant's argument
Find the initial legal analogy: what is the claimed ruling and on what basis? The text states: 'it is not permissible to marry a slave woman just as if he had a free wife under him.' This is a qiyas: the ruling of forbidding marrying a slave woman is extended from the case of having a free wife.
2
Extract the Maliki's response (mu'tarid)
The Maliki objects by saying that one should not initiate ta'wil (interpretation) of the apparent meaning nor takhsis (specification) of the general by qiyas. This is a methodological objection: the qiyas is invalid because it would improperly change the clear text.
The Maliki is not directly refuting the qiyas but arguing that qiyas cannot override textual principles.
3
Identify al-Baji's critique of the Maliki's response
Al-Baji states that this type of answer is not correct. He is critiquing the Maliki's response itself, not the original qiyas. This shows that even a response can be flawed if it does not follow proper dialectical procedure.
4
Assess the dialectical outcome
According to the rules of jadal, if al-Baji's critique is accepted, the Maliki's response is invalid. The original claimant (the one making the qiyas) would not be refuted by that response. The debate would continue with a better response needed.
This highlights the importance of dialectical competence: a weak response can be worse than no response.

الجدل 357 بنكاح ، فلم يجز نكاح أمة كما لو كانت تحته حرة. والطريق في الجواب عن ذلك أن يتكلم المالكي على القياس، بأن يقول مثلا بعدم جواز ابتداء تأويل الظاهر ولا تخصيص العموم بالقياس، لكن الباجي يرى أن هذا النوع من الجواب ليس بصحيح (1) *** (1) المنهاج في ترتيب الحجاج، للباجي، ص: 74
With marriage, it is not permissible to marry a slave woman just as if he had a free wife under him. The method in answering that is that the Maliki speaks about the analogy, by saying for example, it is not permissible to initiate interpretation of the apparent meaning nor to specify the general by analogy, but al-Baji holds that this type of answer is not correct. (1) *** (1) Al-Minhaj fi Tartib al-Hujaj, by al-Baji, p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical exchange concerning a legal analogy (qiyas) regarding marriage. The argument is that if a man has a free wife, he cannot marry a slave woman, using the analogy of the free wife's status. The Maliki response is to argue that one should not begin with ta'wil (interpretation) of the apparent meaning or takhsis (specification) of the general by qiyas. However, al-Baji critiques this response, stating it is not valid. This illustrates the methodological disagreements among usuliyyun in dialectical practice.

Four Types of Objections to Sunnah Inference in Jadal
Author lists four types of objections to Sunnah inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the four categories of objections against inference from the Sunnah in usul al-fiqh jadal.

Core Idea
Objections to Sunnah go beyond chain criticism to text, cause, and prophetic actions.

This passage marks the beginning of the discussion on jadal specifically concerning the Prophetic Sunnah. The author affirms the Sunnah as the second source of legislation but notes that inferences from it were not always agreed upon. He then classifies objections into four distinct types. Understanding this classification is essential for analyzing juristic debates that involve hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of jadal regarding Sunnah
The author explains that despite the Sunnah's authoritative status, inferences from it are often disputed due to lack of clarity, weak attribution, or interpretative possibilities. This sets the stage for diverse objections.
2
List the four categories from the passage
From the Arabic, extract the four types: (1) objections attacking the chain (isnad), (2) objections to the text (matn) of the hadith, (3) objections concerning hadith with a specific cause (sabab), and (4) objections regarding the actions of the Prophet (af'al).
The author groups matn objections as similar to those against the Qur'an.
3
Distinguish between isnad and matn objections
Isnad objections question the reliability or continuity of the narrators. Matn objections question the meaning, clarity, or implication of the hadith text. These require different responses in jadal.
4
Recognize the unique category of af'al al-Nabi
Prophetic actions are not verbal reports; their legal implications (command, recommendation, permissibility) are debated. Objections here often concern whether the action indicates obligation or mere permission.
5
Connect to broader jadal framework
The author will treat each type separately. This classification helps usuliyyun structure their debates and respond precisely to each objection type.
This taxonomy is a tool for systematic argumentation.

توطئة : الفصل الثاني الجدل في الاستدلال بالسنة السنة النبوية الشريفة هي المصدر الثاني للتشريع بعد القرآن الكريم، فهي الملاذ الذي يرجع إليه الباحثون في العلوم الشرعية عندما لا يقفون في القرآن على دليل لما يدعونه من آراء في مسألة من مسائل العلوم الشرعية التي يبحثونها . وقد كثر الاستدلال من السنة الشريفة، واتفق الباحثون والعلماء على الاستدلال بها لما ينتهون إليه من ،آراء، لكن هذه الاستدلالات لم تكن دائما محل تسليم بينهم، حيث إن الدليل لا يكون عادة صريحًا في دلالته على معناه، أو ربما كان صريحا لكنه غير ثابت النسبة إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، أو يتطرق الاحتمال إلى معناه أو ما إلى ذلك . لذلك وجدنا أن الجدل قد دار حول الاستدلال بالسنة بين الأصوليين في جزئيات المسائل خاصة وتنوعت الاعتراضات التي يتوجه بها إلى الاستدلال بهذا الدليل الشرعي من هذه الجهة : - فهي إما اعتراضات من جهة الطعن في الإسناد. - أو اعتراضات على الاستدلال بمتن السنة وهي اعتراضات لا تختلف عن تلك التي تناولناها عند الحديث عن الاعتراضات التي يتوجه بها على الاستدلال بالكتاب . - أو اعتراضات على الاستدلال بالسنة الواردة على سبب - أو اعتراضات على الاستدلال بأفعال النبي . ونتناول فيما يلي كل نوع من هذه الاعتراضات، في مبحث مستقل .
Prefatory note: Chapter Two - Jadal in inference from the Sunnah. The noble prophetic Sunnah is the second source of legislation after the Noble Qur'an. It is the refuge to which researchers in the religious sciences return when they do not find in the Qur'an evidence for the opinions they claim in any issue of the religious sciences they investigate. Inference from the noble Sunnah has been abundant, and researchers and scholars have agreed upon inferring by it for the opinions they conclude. However, these inferences were not always a point of agreement among them, because the evidence is usually not explicit in its indication of its meaning, or perhaps it is explicit but its attribution to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is not established, or probability enters its meaning, or something similar. Therefore, we found that jadal has taken place regarding inference from the Sunnah among the usuliyyun, especially in particular issues, and the objections directed at inference by this legal evidence from this aspect are diverse: They are either objections from the angle of attacking the chain (isnad), or objections to inference from the text (matn) of the Sunnah – and these objections do not differ from those we discussed when talking about objections directed at inference from the Book – or objections to inference from the Sunnah that occurred on a specific cause (sabab), or objections to inference from the actions of the Prophet (af'al al-Nabi). We will address each type of these objections in a separate section.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is an introductory preface to the discussion of jadal (dialectical argumentation) specifically concerning inference from the Prophetic Sunnah. The author begins by affirming the Sunnah's role as the second source of legislation after the Qur'an, emphasizing its importance for scholars seeking evidence not explicitly found in the Qur'an. Despite the widespread acceptance of using the Sunnah for deriving rulings, the author notes that such inferences were not always undisputed. The reasons include lack of clarity in the text's indication, questionable attribution to the Prophet, or potential for alternative interpretations. The author then lists four distinct categories of objections that arise in this context: (1) objections attacking the chain of transmission (isnad), (2) objections to the content of the hadith (matn) – which are similar to objections against Qur'anic verses, (3) objections concerning hadith that were revealed on a specific occasion (sabab), and (4) objections regarding the actions of the Prophet (af'al). The passage concludes by stating that each type will be examined in its own section. The structure sets up a systematic treatment of these objections, which is typical in usul al-fiqh works on jadal.

Objecting to a Hadith's Chain in Jadal
Author discusses objection demanding proof of chain for non-canonical hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a chain authentication objection is appropriate in a legal debate and formulate the correct response by either providing the chain or referring to a canonical collection.

Core Idea
The chain objection is only valid for non-canonical hadiths; the answer is to cite a known authentic source.

In legal debates, opponents often challenge the authenticity of hadiths used as evidence. This lesson focuses on the first type of such objection: demanding proof of the chain of transmission. The author distinguishes between hadiths found in canonical collections (Sahihs, Sunans) and those only transmitted by opponents. You will learn the proper way to respond to this objection, as practised in usul al-fiqh jadal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection type
The objection is 'demanding authentication of the chain' (al-mutalabah bi-tashih al-isnad). It targets the reliability of the hadith's transmission, not its meaning.
2
Assess the appropriateness of the objection
The author states this objection is not suitable for hadiths in Sahihs and famous Sunans. It is only relevant for hadiths not recorded there and only heard from opponents.
Check if the hadith is from al-Muwatta’, Sahih al-Bukhari, Sahih Muslim, or a famous Sunan.
3
Examine the Hanafi examples
Two examples are given: a hadith about zakat on cows (including the phrase 'and whatever increases, by its calculation') and a hadith about khul‘ divorce. The author implies these are not from canonical collections, so the objection is valid.
The footnotes show the phrase 'by its calculation' is baseless.
4
Formulate the proper response
The arguer (al-mustadill) must clarify the chain or refer to a famous book whose compiler authenticated hadiths, such as al-Muwatta’, Sahih al-Bukhari, or the Sunan. Referring to books that mix authentic and weak hadiths (e.g., some later compilations) is insufficient.
The response must provide a clear, verifiable source.
5
Understand the jadal principle
This shows that in dialectical debate, objections must be well-founded. The objector must know when their challenge is valid, and the responder must know how to counter it using recognized sources.

المبحث الأول الاعتراض على الاستدلال بالسنة من جهة الإسناد الاعتراض على أسانيد الأخبار إنما يكون من وجهين : المطلب الأول : من جهة المطالبة بتصحيح الإسناد وإثباته وهذا النوع من الاعتراض لا يليق الاتجاه به إلى الأحاديث والسنن الثابتة في الصحاح والسنن المشهورة ودواوين الحديث المعروفة وإنما يليق إبداؤه فيما الأحاديث غير المدونة في السنن والصحاح، ولم تسمع إلا من كان من المخالفين . ومثال هذا النوع من الأحاديث : ما استدل به الحنفية في نصاب زكاة البقر وما يجب إخراجه منها، من نقل لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: (في أربعين مسنة، وفيما زاد فبحسابه) (1) ، ومنها أيضًا ما استدلوا به في شأن طلاق المختلعة، حيث نسبوا إلى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه قال : المختلعة يلحقها الطلاق ما دامت في العدة) (2) ، وغير ذلك من الأخبار التي من هذا القبيل. والطريق في الجواب عن هذا الاعتراض أن يبين المستدل إسناد ما استدل به أو يحيل على كتاب مشهور اشترط صاحبه الصحة واعتمد مؤلفه صحيح الحديث واشتهر بذلك، مثل أن يحيل إلى الموطأ أو أحد الصحيحين أو كتب السنن المشهورة، فإن أحال على الكتب التي تجمع الصحيح وغير الصحيح لم يثبت (1) عن معاذ بن جبل قال : بعثني النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى اليمن، فأمرني أن آخذ من كل ثلاثين بقرة تبيعا أو تبيعة ، ومن أربعين مسنة ، ومن كل حالم دينارا أو عدله معافر ، أخرجه أبو داود في سننه، كتاب الزكاة ، رقم : 1345 ، والترمذي في سننه ، كتاب الزكاة عن رسول الله، باب ما جاء في زكاة البقر، رقم 566 ورقم : 623 ، وابن ماجه في سننه كتاب الزكاة، رقم: 173 ، وعبارة وما زاد فبحسابه لا أصل لها في كتب الحديث انظر نصب الراية، للزيلعي ، ج: 2، ص : 346 - 353 . - (2) في سنن البيهقي كتاب الخلع والطلاق باب المختلعة لا يلحقها الطلاق (ج 7، ص : 317) إشارة إلى هذا الحديث، وقد قال ابن قدامة في الرد على من قال بموجبه : وحديثهم لا نعرف له أصلا، ولا ذكره أصحاب السنن ) (المغني، ج 7، ص : 59) .
First section: Objection to inference from the Sunnah from the angle of the chain (isnad). Objection to the chains of traditions is only from two aspects: First demand: from the angle of demanding the authentication of the chain and its proof. This type of objection is not appropriate to direct at the hadiths and sunan established in the Sahihs, famous Sunans, and well-known hadith collections; rather, it is appropriate to raise it regarding hadiths not recorded in the Sunans and Sahihs, and which are only heard from those who are opponents. An example of this type of hadiths is what the Hanafis used as evidence regarding the nisab (minimum threshold) of zakat on cows and what must be paid from it, from a report of the Prophet's saying: 'For every forty (cows) a mature cow (musinnah), and for whatever increases, by its calculation' (1). Also among them is what they used as evidence concerning the divorce of a woman who seeks khul‘ (mukhtali‘ah), attributing to the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'The mukhtali‘ah is subject to divorce as long as she is in the waiting period ('iddah)' (2), and other reports of this kind. The way to answer this objection is for the arguer to clarify the chain of what he has used as evidence or to refer to a famous book whose author stipulated authenticity and relied on authentic hadith and became well known for that, such as referring to al-Muwatta’, one of the two Sahihs, or the famous Sunan books. If he refers to books that collect authentic and non-authentic materials, it is not established. (Footnote 1): From Mu‘adh ibn Jabal, he said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) sent me to Yemen, and he ordered me to take from every thirty cows a tabi‘ or tabi‘ah, and from forty a musinnah, and from every adult a dinar or its equivalent in ma‘afir. Reported by Abu Dawud in his Sunan, Book of Zakat, no. 1345; al-Tirmidhi in his Sunan, Book of Zakat, Chapter on what came about zakat on cows, no. 566 and no. 623; Ibn Majah in his Sunan, Book of Zakat, no. 173. The phrase 'and what increases by its calculation' has no basis in hadith books. See Nasb al-Rayah, al-Zayla‘i, vol. 2, pp. 346-353. - (Footnote 2): In Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Khul‘ and Divorce, Chapter: The mukhtali‘ah is not subject to divorce (vol. 7, p. 317), there is a reference to this hadith. Ibn Qudamah said in refutation of those who act according to it: 'Their hadith is unknown to us, and the authors of the Sunan did not mention it.' (al-Mughni, vol. 7, p. 59).
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of the first type of objection against inference from the Sunnah, namely, objections concerning the chain of transmission (isnad). The author identifies two aspects of such objections; here he focuses on the first aspect: demanding that the chain be authenticated and proven. The key point is that this objection is not appropriate for hadiths found in the canonical collections (Sahihs, Sunans, etc.) whose authenticity is widely accepted. Rather, it is relevant only for hadiths that are not recorded in those famous books and are transmitted solely by opponents. The author provides two examples from Hanafi arguments: one regarding the zakat threshold for cows (a hadith about taking a musinnah for forty cows and a calculation for increases) and another about divorce of a woman who seeks khul‘ (a hadith stating that she is subject to divorce during the 'iddah). For the first example, the footnote indicates that the specific phrase 'and what increases by its calculation' is not found in standard hadith collections. The second example is rejected by scholars like Ibn Qudamah as unknown. The proper response to this objection, the author explains, is for the arguer (al-mustadill) to either provide the complete chain of the hadith or to refer to a well-known book whose compiler is known for rigorous authentication, such as al-Muwatta’, Sahih al-Bukhari, Sahih Muslim, or the Sunan collections. Simply referring to books that mix authentic and weak hadiths (like some later compilations) does not suffice. This section illustrates how jadal in usul al-fiqh operates: the opponent raises a specific objection, and the proponent must answer with a clear methodological response.

Responding to Chain Objections in Dialectical Debate
Author explains objection type demanding chain confirmation and how to respond.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether an objection to a hadith's chain is appropriate in a jadal setting, and construct the proper response as a mustadill using the author's three methods.

Core Idea
Objecting to a hadith's chain is only valid for obscure reports, not for well-known ones accepted by the ummah.

In jadal (dialectical debate) within usul al-fiqh, objectors often attack the sunnah evidence by demanding proof of its chain. However, this objection is not always legitimate. The author of our passage distinguishes between famous, well-established hadiths and obscure ones, and provides the adducer (mustadill) with clear strategies to respond. This lesson will help you navigate this common dialectical move with precision and confidence.

Guided Path
1
Classify the hadith's fame
First, determine whether the hadith is recorded in famous authentic collections (Sahihayn, Muwatta', Sunan) or is widely known and accepted by the community. If yes, the objection demanding chain is inappropriate.
The author gives examples like 'Actions are by intentions' and the Prophet wiping his head in wudu.
2
Assess the objector's standing
If the objector insists on demanding chain for a famous hadith, note that this indicates weakness in debate (da'f fi al-jadal). The mustadill can point this out without getting into chain details.
3
Choose the appropriate response
For obscure hadiths, the mustadill must either: (1) clarify the chain, (2) refer to a famous book whose author stipulated authenticity, or (3) if the hadith is still not famous, he cannot simply rely on fame. For famous hadiths, the response is to invoke shuhrah and the ummah's acceptance.
4
Apply the rule to your own debate
When you encounter a chain objection in jadal, identify which category the hadith falls into and then follow the corresponding response strategy.
The author emphasizes that the mustadill can also mention that scholars differed in understanding the hadith, but all agreed on its chain.

المبحث الأول
الاعتراض على الاستدلال بالسنة من جهة الإسناد
الاعتراض على أسانيد الأخبار إنما يكون من وجهين :
المطلب الأول : من جهة المطالبة بتصحيح الإسناد وإثباته
وهذا النوع من الاعتراض لا يليق الاتجاه به إلى الأحاديث والسنن الثابتة في الصحاح والسنن المشهورة ودواوين الحديث المعروفة وإنما يليق إبداؤه فيما الأحاديث غير المدونة في السنن والصحاح، ولم تسمع إلا من كان من المخالفين .
ومثال هذا النوع من الأحاديث : ما استدل به الحنفية في نصاب زكاة البقر وما يجب إخراجه منها، من نقل لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: (في أربعين مسنة، وفيما زاد فبحسابه) ، ومنها أيضًا ما استدلوا به في شأن طلاق المختلعة، حيث نسبوا إلى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه قال : المختلعة يلحقها الطلاق ما دامت في العدة) ، وغير ذلك من الأخبار التي من هذا القبيل.
والطريق في الجواب عن هذا الاعتراض أن يبين المستدل إسناد ما استدل به أو يحيل على كتاب مشهور اشترط صاحبه الصحة واعتمد مؤلفه صحيح الحديث واشتهر بذلك، مثل أن يحيل إلى الموطأ أو أحد الصحيحين أو كتب السنن المشهورة، فإن أحال على الكتب التي تجمع الصحيح وغير الصحيح لم يثبت حديثه بذلك ولم يقبل منه الاحتجاج به أما إن كان الحديث المستدل به مشهورًا ومنتشرًا ومعلوم الصحة، فإنه يستغنى عن طلب إسناده لشهرته، وذلك كاستدلال الفقيه المالكي مثلا بحديث (إنما الأعمال بالنيات) ، أو بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح جميع رأسه في الوضوء ، فلا يحسن بالمعترض أن يطالب المستدل بإثبات الإسناد في مثل هذه الأحاديث، فإن فعل كان ذلك دليلا على ضعفه في الجدل وتعلقه بما لا فائدة من التعلق به، لكن إن حصل هذا النوع من الاعتراض فإن للمستدل أن يجيب بأن الأمة قد تلقت هذه الأحاديث بالقبول، إلا أن من العلماء من عمل بها، ومنهم من تأولها، وصحة الإسناد محل إجماع .
The first topic: Objection to relying on sunnah from the aspect of chain. Objection to chains of reports is from two aspects: The first aspect: from the aspect of demanding correction and proof of the chain. This type of objection is not appropriate to direct to the hadiths and sunnahs established in the authentic collections, well-known sunan, and famous hadith compilations; rather, it is appropriate to raise it regarding hadiths not recorded in the sunan and authentic collections, and which have only been heard from opponents. An example of this type of hadith: what the Hanafis adduced regarding the nisab of zakat on cows and what must be given from them, from a report of the Prophet's saying: 'For every forty a musinnah, and for what increases, according to its calculation.' Also from it is what they adduced concerning the divorce of al-mukhtali'ah, where they attributed to the Prophet that he said: 'The mukhtali'ah is subject to divorce as long as she is in the waiting period.' And other reports of this kind. The method of answering this objection is that the adducer should clarify the chain of what he adduced, or refer to a famous book whose author stipulated authenticity and relied on authentic hadiths and became famous for that, such as referring to al-Muwatta', or one of the two Sahihs, or the well-known books of Sunan. If he refers to books that gather authentic and non-authentic, his hadith is not proven by that and his argumentation is not accepted. But if the adduced hadith is famous, widespread, and known to be authentic, then it suffices to ask for its chain due to its fame, such as the Malikite jurist's adducing the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' or that the Prophet wiped all of his head in ablution. It is not proper for the objector to demand proof of the chain in such hadiths; if he does, that is evidence of his weakness in debate and his clinging to what there is no benefit in clinging to. However, if this type of objection occurs, the adducer can answer that the community has received these hadiths with acceptance, even though some scholars acted on them and others interpreted them, and the authenticity of the chain is a matter of consensus.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is from a work on jadal (dialectics) for usul al-fiqh. It classifies objections to sunnah evidence into two types, focusing here on the first: demanding proof of the chain. The author states that such an objection is inappropriate for well-known hadiths in authoritative collections like Sahihayn, Muwatta', and Sunan. It is only legitimate for hadiths that are obscure or transmitted only by opponents. He gives examples from Hanafi fiqh about the nisab of cows and divorce of mukhtali'ah. The response (jawab) for the adducer is either to present the chain, refer to a famous authentic book, or if the hadith is widely known, point to its fame and the community's acceptance. The passage emphasizes that objectors who demand chains for famous hadiths show weakness in debate. It provides three levels of response: (1) clarifying the chain, (2) referring to a known authentic compilation, or (3) invoking the hadith's fame and the ummah's acceptance. The last response includes citing that some scholars acted on it and others interpreted it, but the authenticity of the chain is agreed upon.

المُعترض
المستدل
الشهرة

Key Takeaway
In jadal, chain objections are only legitimate for obscure hadiths; for famous ones, the mustadill can invoke shuhrah and community acceptance.

Three Ways to Attack the Chain of Transmission in Dialectical Debate
Author enumerates three forms of challenging hadith chains in jadal: accusing narrator of lying, innovation, or frequent error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three valid grounds for attacking a narrator's reliability in a dialectical debate and evaluate whether a specific objection is permissible under jadal rules.

Core Idea
In jadal, you can't just dismiss a narrator; you must specify a defect supported by scholarly consensus.

In this passage from the science of jadal, the author classifies the legitimate ways to impugn a hadith chain in debate. You will learn the three recognized grounds—lying, innovation, and frequent error—and see concrete examples from actual fiqh disputes. Mastering this allows you to use hadith criticism accurately within the rules of dialectical exchange.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the context of jadal
The passage is part of a work on debate rules. The author explains how to respond when an opponent cites a hadith. The response must attack the chain, not just the content.
2
Identify the three categories
The author lists: (1) accusing a narrator of lying, (2) attacking his religion (innovation), (3) pointing out frequent error/heedlessness. Each has a different basis: truthfulness, religious integrity, memory.
3
Examine the examples for each category
For liar: Ibrahim ibn Isma'il and Baraka al-Halabi are condemned by scholars. For innovator: Ma'bad al-Juhani as a Qadari. For error: the witr hadith example implies the narrator is prone to error.
4
Understand the procedural requirement
The objection must be supported by the consensus of hadith scholars (e.g., 'a group of hadith scholars have said'). Not just any accusation; it must have backing.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical debate, decide which of the three grounds could be invoked and whether it meets the standard of scholarly support.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني : من جهة القدح والتجريح في الإسناد وذلك من ثلاثة أوجه :
1 - أن يطعن في الراوي بأمر يوجب رد حديثه : كأن يتهمه بالكذب أو البدعة أو الغفلة .
أولها : أن يقول عن الراوي أنه كذاب ومثاله أن يستدل الشافعي في قتل من وقع على بهيمة بما روي عن النبي الله أنه قال : «من وقع على بهيمة فاقتلوه واقتلوا البهيمة» فيعترض عليه المالكي ويقول : هذا الحديث يرويه إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن أبي حبيبة المدني، وقد قال جماعة من أصحاب الحديث : «هو كذاب يضع الحديث» ومثله كذلك أن يستدل بما رواه بركة بن محمد الحلبي عن يوسف بن أسباط عن سفيان الثوري عن خالد الحذاء عن ابن سيرين عن أبي هريرة، أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم جعل المضمضة والاستنشاق للجنب ثلاثا فريضة، مسنونتان في الوضوء حيث قال أصحاب الحديث بركة الحلبي كذاب يضع الحديث.
ثانيها : أن يذكر طعنًا في دينه يوجب بدعته، فيوجب ذلك رد حديثه ؛ مثل أن يستدل أصحاب أبي حنيفة في مسألة القهقهة في الصلاة بما روى معبد الجهني أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أمر من قهقه خلفه بإعادة الوضوء والصلاة فيعترضه المالكي بأن يقول : هذا الحديث يرويه معبد الجهني، وهو قدري داعية، فلا يصح الاحتجاج به.
ثالثها: أن يذكر أنه معروف بكثرة الخطأ والغفلة مثل أن يستدل الحنفي في وجوب الوتر، بما روي عن النبي الله أنه قال : «إن الله زادكم صلاة إلى صلواتكم وهي الوتر».
The second demand: Regarding the aspect of disparagement and impugning in the chain of transmission, and that is from three aspects:
1 - That he attacks the narrator with something that necessitates rejecting his hadith: such as accusing him of lying, innovation, or heedlessness.
The first of them: That he says about the narrator that he is a liar. Its example is that al-Shafi‘i argues in [the case of] killing one who fell upon an animal by what was narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'Whoever falls upon an animal, kill him and kill the animal.' Then the Maliki objects to him and says: This hadith is narrated by Ibrahim ibn Isma‘il ibn Abi Habiba al-Madani, and a group of hadith scholars have said: 'He is a liar who fabricates hadith.' Similarly, that he argues by what was narrated by Baraka ibn Muhammad al-Halabi from Yusuf ibn Asbat from Sufyan al-Thawri from Khalid al-Hadhdha’ from Ibn Sirin from Abu Hurayra, that the Prophet ﷺ made rinsing the mouth and sniffing water for the junub three times obligatory, two sunnas in ablution – whereas the hadith scholars said: Baraka al-Halabi is a liar who fabricates hadith.
The second: That he mentions an attack on his religion that necessitates his innovation, thus necessitating rejection of his hadith; such as the followers of Abu Hanifa arguing in the issue of laughing out loud in prayer by what Ma‘bad al-Juhani narrated that the Prophet ﷺ ordered one who laughed out loud behind him to repeat ablution and prayer. Then the Maliki objects to him by saying: This hadith is narrated by Ma‘bad al-Juhani, and he is a Qadari who calls [to it], so it is not valid to use it as evidence.
The third: That he mentions that he is known for frequent error and heedlessness, such as the Hanafi arguing for the obligation of witr by what was narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'Indeed Allah has added a prayer to your prayers, and it is witr.'
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a classification from the science of jadal (dialectical debate), specifically addressing how to attack the chain of transmission (isnad) of a hadith presented by an opponent. The author states that there are three ways to invalidate a hadith by attacking its chain, each dealing with a defect in the narrator. 

First, the opponent can accuse the narrator of being a liar. Two examples are given: in the first, al-Shafi‘i uses a hadith about executing someone who commits bestiality; the Maliki opponent responds that the narrator, Ibrahim ibn Isma‘il, is known by scholars to be a liar who fabricates hadith. In the second example, a hadith about rinsing the mouth and sniffing water for the ritually impure is cited, but the narrator Baraka al-Halabi is similarly accused of fabrication.

Second, the opponent can attack the narrator's religious integrity, specifically accusing him of innovation (bid‘a) that renders him unreliable. The example involves Abu Hanifa’s school arguing that laughing out loud in prayer nullifies ablution, based on a hadith from Ma‘bad al-Juhani. The Maliki opponent points out that Ma‘bad was a Qadari (a deviant sect) and a proponent, so his narration is not acceptable.

Third, the opponent can claim that the narrator is known for frequent mistakes and heedlessness. The example is a Hanafi argument that witr prayer is obligatory, citing a hadith about Allah adding a prayer. The missing response is not detailed here, but the principle is that a narrator prone to error cannot be relied upon.

The passage demonstrates that in jadal, attacks on the chain must be substantive and based on established scholarly criticism, not mere dismissal.

Key Terms
القدح
التجريح
الإسناد

C) The narrator is known for frequent errors and heedlessness.
D) The hadith is not narrated continuously.

Key Takeaway
The three valid grounds for attacking a narrator in jadal are lying, innovation, and frequent error, and each must be supported by scholarly criticism.
